2:29:1896:0:14:72:288:700:12:Times:12:Times:C:Firm Selection and Corporate Cash Holdings
2:30:1938:14:14:72:263:686:12:Times:12:Times:C:Juliane Begenau and Berardino Palazzo
2:31:1975:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:C:NBER Working Paper No. 23249
2:32:2003:14:14:72:130:658:12:Times:12:Times:C:March 2017
2:33:2013:14:28:72:164:644:12:Times:12:Times:C:JEL No. E3,G1,G3
2:34:2029:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:C:ABSTRACT
2:35:2037:28:14:72:546:588:12:Times:12:Times:C:Among  stock  market  entrants,  more  firms  over  time  are  R&D–intensive  with  initially  lower 
2:36:2138:14:14:72:546:574:12:Times:12:Times:C:profitability but higher growth potential. This sample-selection effect determines the secular trend 
2:37:2238:14:14:72:546:560:12:Times:12:Times:C:in  U.S.  public firms’  cash  holdings.  A  stylized  firm  industry  model  allows  us  to  analyze  two 
2:38:2344:14:14:72:546:546:12:Times:12:Times:C:competing  changes to  the  selection  mechanism:  a  change  in  industry  composition  and  a  shift 
2:39:2446:14:14:72:545:532:12:Times:12:Times:C:toward  less  profitable  R&D–firms. The  latter  is  key  to  generating  higher  cash  ratios  at  IPO, 
2:40:2551:14:14:72:545:518:12:Times:12:Times:C:necessary for the secular increase, whereas the former mechanism amplifies this effect. The data 
2:41:2647:14:42:72:497:504:12:Times:12:Times:C:confirm the prominent role played by selection, and corroborate the model’s predictions.
2:42:2734:42:14:72:151:462:12:Times:12:Times:C:Juliane Begenau
2:43:2749:14:14:72:193:448:12:Times:12:Times:C:Harvard Business School
2:44:2772:14:14:72:161:434:12:Times:12:Times:C:Baker Library 365
2:45:2789:14:14:72:139:420:12:Times:12:Times:C:Soldiers Field
2:46:2803:14:14:72:164:406:12:Times:12:Times:C:Boston, MA 02163
2:47:2819:14:14:72:124:392:12:Times:12:Times:C:and NBER
2:48:2827:14:28:72:163:378:12:Times:12:Times:C:jbegenau@hbs.edu

3:52:2892:0:36:72:208:721:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:1    Introduction
3:53:2909:36:24:89:539:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:TheaverageU.S. public firm has changed its characteristics over the last 35 years.  The
3:54:2996:24:24:72:540:661:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:disappearance  of  dividends  (Fama  and  French  (2001)),  the  decline  in  profitability  (Fama
3:55:3094:24:24:72:540:637:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and  French  (2004)),  the  increase  in  cash  holdings  (Bates  et  al.  (2009))  and  firm-specific
3:56:3196:24:23:72:540:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:risk measures (Davis et al. (2007) and Brown and Kapadia (2007)) are phenomena of this
3:57:3282:23:24:72:540:590:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:period.  A change in the behavior of the average public firm could be caused by a change in
3:58:3373:24:24:72:540:566:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the behavior of incumbent firms as well as by the selection of a different type of firm into
3:59:3465:24:24:72:421:542:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the stock market that gradually replaces incumbent firms over time.
3:60:3532:24:24:89:539:518:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:This  paper  studies  and  quantifies  the  role  of  sample  selection  for  the  secular  increase
3:61:3632:24:24:72:539:494:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the average cash–to–assets ratio of U.S. public companies over the last 35 years.1The
3:62:3720:24:24:72:540:470:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:following facts motivate our research.  Since the beginning of the 1980s, firms went public
3:63:3811:24:24:72:540:446:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with progressively higher cash–to–assets ratios, but they reduced their cash ratios gradually
3:64:3904:24:24:72:540:422:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:afterward (see Figure 1).2This feature of the data is indicative of a sample-selection mecha-
3:65:3997:24:24:72:540:398:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:nism, namely, a change in the conditions that determine which firms choose to enter the stock
3:66:4090:24:24:72:539:374:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:market.  Figure 2shows that at least two features of entering cohorts have changed over time,
3:67:4183:24:23:72:540:350:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:pointing to two different selection mechanisms.  First, the share of R&D–intensive firms in
3:68:4274:23:24:72:540:327:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:U.S. public markets has increased substantially due to a growing fraction of R&D–intensive
3:69:4364:24:24:72:540:303:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:newly listed firms (left panel).  Second, R&D–intensive firms have entered with progressively
3:70:4457:24:24:72:540:279:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:higher cash balances (right panel), suggesting a change in the type of R&D–intensive stock
3:71:4547:24:24:72:157:255:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:market entrants.
3:72:4563:24:24:89:539:231:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The compositional change of U.S. public companies corresponds to a shift in the com-
3:73:4647:24:24:72:540:207:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:position  of  the  overall  U.S.  economy  toward  R&D–intensive  firms.3For  example,Halti-
3:74:4739:24:18:72:539:183:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wanger,  Hathaway,  and Miranda(2014) document a significant increase in the number of
3:75:4825:18:16:85:539:165:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:1We  report  the  evolution  of  the  average  cash–to–assets  ratio  of  U.S.  listed  firms  during  the  period
3:76:4939:16:8:72:187:149:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:1958–2014 in AppendixB.

3:81:5401:12:8:71:343:89:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:is the average cash–to–assets ratio of incumbent firms in 1958.

5:130:7386:24:24:89:539:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The  increase  in  cash  holdings  of  newly  listed  R&D–intensive  firms  suggests  each  new
5:131:7481:24:23:72:540:625:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cohort to the stock market has different characteristics.  Indeed, over time newly listed firms
5:132:7576:23:24:72:540:602:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are  smaller,  less  profitable,  and  appear  to  exhibit  higher  cash-flow  volatility  compared  to
5:133:7679:24:24:72:540:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:previous cohorts.  In the spirit ofFama and French(2004), the selection of a different type
5:134:7770:24:24:72:540:554:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of firm could be driven by more favorable IPO conditions that have allowedweakerfirms to
5:135:7858:24:24:72:539:530:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:go public (i.e.,“a downward shift in the supply curve for new list equity funding” Fama and
5:136:7949:24:24:72:540:506:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:French(2004,  page 233)).  Such a change could have been instigated by the relaxation of
5:137:8037:24:24:72:540:482:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the Employment Retirement Income Security Act’s (ERISA) “Prudent Man” Rule passed by
5:138:8121:24:24:72:540:458:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Congress in 1979 that induced pension funds to invest in riskier (i.e., smaller, less profitable,
5:139:8218:24:24:72:540:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and higher growth option) ventures.4The ensuing improvement in IPO conditions for risky
5:140:8305:24:24:72:516:410:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:firms might have particularly benefited R&D–intensive firms, as indicated by Figure2.
5:141:8390:24:24:89:539:386:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In the first part of this paper, we build a stylized firm industry model with endogenous
5:142:8478:24:23:72:540:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:entry to gain insights into how these two selection mechanisms can shape the secular increase
5:143:8571:23:24:72:540:339:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in cash holdings. The benefit of a model is that we can isolate confounding effects and develop
5:144:8666:24:24:72:540:315:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:testable predictions.  In the second part of the paper, we test whether the data corroborate
5:145:8758:24:24:72:194:291:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the model’s predictions.
5:146:8782:24:24:89:539:267:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Our firm industry model assumes firms belong to two sectors that share the same pro-
5:147:8866:24:24:72:540:243:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:duction  technology  and  financing  opportunities.   We  interpret  old-economy  firms  as  non-
5:148:8963:24:24:72:540:219:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:R&D–intensive and new-economy firms as R&D–intensive.  Guided by the evidence in Fig-
5:149:9048:24:18:72:540:195:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ure2, we assume that only firms in the new-economy sector experience an improvement in
5:150:9134:18:15:85:540:177:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f9:F:4As noted inLongstreth(1987, page 101)“The Venture Capital and Innovation Study prepared in 1984
5:151:9230:15:12:71:539:162:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:F:for  the  Joint  Economic  Committee  of  the  Congress  reports  that  63.5  percent  of  the  venture  capital  firms
5:152:9349:12:12:71:539:150:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:F:consulted believed there was a bias among institutional investors against investing in small businesses, with
5:153:9458:12:12:71:539:138:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:F:the leading causes being a lack of institutional expertise in small business investing and the ”excessive risk-
5:154:9569:12:12:71:539:126:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:F:adverse behavior of institutional investors.” While perhaps itself biased, this view lends some support to the
5:155:9679:12:12:71:539:114:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:F:idea that the prudent man rule exerts a restraining influence.  More tel ling was the study’s findings (a) that
5:156:9790:12:12:71:539:102:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:F:the liberalizing regulations issued by the Labor Department in June 1979 were a ”major factor” in the surge
5:157:9897:12:12:71:539:90:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:F:of  pension  fund  investment  in  venture  capital  after  that  date,  and  (b)  that  the  uncertainties  of  the  federal
5:158:10022:12:12:71:539:78:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:F:prudent  man  rule  contained  in  ERISA,  including  the  possibility  of  being  judged  investment-by-investment,
5:159:10138:12:12:71:539:66:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:F:may  have  contributed  to  a  shift  toward  greater  risk  aversion  by  pension  fund  fiduciaries  from  1974,  when
5:160:10258:12:0:71:354:54:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:F:ERISA was enacted, until the interpretative regulations of 1979.”
6:161:10324:0:24:72:540:721:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the conditions that influence their entry decisions.  A reduction in entry costs causes firms
6:162:10417:24:24:72:540:697:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with lower idiosyncratic productivity (i.e., less profitable firms with high growth potential)
6:163:10511:24:24:72:540:673:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to go public.  The assumed mean reversion in the productivity process implies these firms
6:164:10600:24:24:72:540:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:have higher funding needs and choose higher cash balances at entry to save up for future
6:165:10688:24:23:72:540:625:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:investment opportunities in order to avoid equity issuance costs.  As these firms grow, they
6:166:10780:23:24:72:540:602:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reduce their cash holdings given that they can rely more on internal funds, thus making the
6:167:10871:24:24:72:315:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model consistent with the evidence in Figure 1.
6:168:10918:24:24:89:539:554:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The model predicts that the first selection mechanism, a change in the industry compo-
6:169:11004:24:24:72:540:530:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sition at entry (across-industryselection),  plays no role in shaping the secular increase in
6:170:11097:24:24:72:540:506:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cash.  However,  it provides an important amplification mechanism when coupled with the
6:171:11184:24:24:72:539:482:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:entry of less-profitable, high-growth-potential new-economy firms (intra-industryselection).
6:172:11276:24:24:72:540:458:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:This second selection effect is necessary to generate increasing cash holdings at entry over
6:173:11368:24:24:72:540:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:time that, in turn, lead to a steady increase in the average cash–to–assets ratio in the cross
6:174:11462:24:24:72:540:410:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:section.  In addition, the model suggests the turnover ratio plays a major role in determining
6:175:11556:24:24:72:540:386:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the  cash  holdings  of  entering  firms  given  its  tight  connection  with  firm-level  profitability
6:176:11660:24:23:72:502:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:since the ratio of sales over total assets is proportional to profitability in the model.
6:177:11749:23:24:89:539:339:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In the second part of the paper, we measure the importance of sample selection in de-
6:178:11834:24:24:72:540:315:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:termining  the  secular  increase  in  cash,  and  test  the  model’s  predictions  in  the  data.   We
6:179:11937:24:24:72:540:291:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:first show that sample selection is a major cause for the secular increase in cash holdings.
6:180:12029:24:24:72:540:267:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Our evidence is straightforward.  On average,  firms deplete their cash holdings over time,
6:181:12120:24:24:72:540:243:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as measured by a negative time trend within firms.  Yet,  on average,  firms’ cash holdings
6:182:12211:24:24:72:540:219:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:have increased.  Thus, the increase in cash holdings is a consequence of newly listed firms
6:183:12302:24:24:72:540:195:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:increasing  their  cash  holdings  at  entry  faster  than  the  rate  at  which  incumbents  deplete
6:184:12403:24:24:72:540:171:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:theirs.  Using a simple accounting identity, we decompose the change in the average cash-to-
6:185:12495:24:24:72:540:147:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:assets ratio over the period 1979–2013 (0.151) in the contribution due to the entry margin
6:186:12585:24:24:72:540:123:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(sample-selection effect) and the contribution due to incumbent firms (within effect).  We
6:187:12675:24:23:72:540:99:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:show  that  sample  selection  accounts  for  more  than  200%  of  the  secular  increase  in  cash
6:188:12775:23:24:72:535:76:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:holdings (0.329), whereas the contribution of the within change is actually -117% (-0.178).
6:189:12866:24:0:89:539:52:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Next, we present evidence for the two selection mechanisms our model highlights.  To this
7:190:12956:0:24:72:540:721:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:end, we construct random subsamples from the data that control for both selection effects
7:191:13045:24:24:72:540:697:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:so that (1) R&D–intensive entrants in the stock market have an average cash–to–assets ratio
7:192:13136:24:24:72:540:673:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as  in  1974-1978  (pre-secular  increase),  and  (2)  the  proportion  of  R&D–intensive  entrants
7:193:13235:24:24:72:540:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is the same as in 1974-1978.  When both restrictions are imposed, we can hardly generate
7:194:13323:24:23:72:540:625:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a positive trend in average cash holdings.  At the same time,  R&D–intensive entrants are
7:195:13412:23:24:72:540:602:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:relatively  larger  and  more  efficient  (i.e.,  higher  turnover  ratio)  compared  to  the  data,  as
7:196:13516:24:24:72:539:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:predicted  by  the  model.   Allowing  for  anacross-industryselection  mechanism  by  lifting
7:197:13610:24:24:72:540:554:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:restriction (2) results in a small increase in average cash holdings that is not large enough
7:198:13703:24:24:72:540:530:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to fit the data.  Moreover,  R&D–intensive entrants are larger and exhibit higher turnover
7:199:13793:24:24:72:540:506:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ratios compared to the actual sample.  Lifting only restriction (1), that is, allowing for an
7:200:13886:24:24:72:540:482:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f3:B:intra-industryselection, results in R&D–intensive entrants whose evolution of characteristics
7:201:13979:24:24:71:539:458:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in terms of size and turnover ratios are in line with the data.  As predicted by the model,
7:202:14070:24:24:71:539:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:average cash holdings increase, but not by as much as to match the data.  For this to happen,
7:203:14163:24:24:71:539:410:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we need to lift both restrictions so that theacross-industryselection mechanism amplifies
7:204:14252:24:24:72:342:386:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the effects of theintra-industryselection mechanism.
7:205:14304:24:23:89:539:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In our model, the turnover ratio is proportional to firm-level productivity and, as such, is
7:206:14396:23:24:72:540:339:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:an important determinant for cash holdings at entry.  We conclude the empirical analysis by
7:207:14487:24:24:72:540:315:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:assessing the explanatory power of the latter variable.  We find the turnover ratio is indeed
7:208:14580:24:24:72:540:291:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:an important predictor of cash holdings at entry, and its dominant explanatory power is not
7:209:14671:24:24:72:540:267:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:subdued when we include a set of important determinants of corporate cash holdings that
7:210:14758:24:24:72:262:243:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:have been discussed in the literature.
7:211:14796:24:24:89:539:219:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Our  paper  contributes  to  the  debate  on  the  causes  of  the  increase  in  cash  holdings
7:212:14892:24:18:72:540:195:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:among  U.S.  publicly  listed  firms.5A  rich  literature  uses  heterogeneous  dynamic  corpo-
7:213:14987:18:15:85:539:177:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:5The literature on the determinants of cash holdings is extensive and ranges over many decades.  A classic
7:214:15093:15:12:72:540:162:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:motive for holding cash is transaction costs (e.g., Baumol (1952), Tobin(1956),Miller and Orr(1966), and
7:215:15197:12:12:72:539:150:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:Vogel and Maddala(1967)).  Other motives include taxes (e.g.,Foley, Hartzell, Titman, and Twite(2007)),
7:216:15300:12:12:72:540:138:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:precautionary savings (e.g.,Froot, Scharfstein, and Stein(1993),Kim et al.(1998)), and agency costs (e.g.,
7:217:15406:12:12:72:539:126:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:Jensen(1986),Dittmar and Mahrt-Smith(2007) andNikolov and Whited(2014)).Opler et al.(1999) provide
7:218:15504:12:12:72:540:114:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:an extensive test of these different motives.  In the last decade,  the secular increase in cash holdings has
7:219:15613:12:12:72:540:102:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:received much attention and spurred many explanations that are not based on sample selection, for example,
7:220:15719:12:12:72:539:90:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:a tax-based explanation byFoley, Hartzell, Titman, and Twite(2007) andFaulkender and Petersen(2012), a
7:221:15821:12:12:72:540:78:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:precautionary savings motive byBates, Kahle, and Stulz(2009),McLean(2011), andZhao(2015), operative
7:222:15920:12:12:72:539:66:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:changes byFalato, Kadyrzhanova, and Sim(2013) andGao(2015), as well as the cost of carrying cash (e.g.
7:223:16022:12:0:72:392:54:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:Azar, Kagy, and Schmalz(2016) andCurtis, Garin, and Mehkari(2015)).
8:224:16090:0:24:72:540:721:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rate finance models to understand and quantify corporate cash policies (e.g.,Gamba and
8:225:16176:24:24:72:540:697:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Triantis(2008),Riddick and Whited(2009),Anderson and Carverhill(2012), andNikolov
8:226:16257:24:24:72:540:673:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and Whited(2014)) as well as the secular increase in cash holdings (e.g.,Falato et al.(2013),
8:227:16350:24:24:72:540:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Gao(2015),Zhao(2015),Armenter and Hnatkovska(2016),Chen et al.(2017)).  The firm’s
8:228:16432:24:23:72:539:625:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:optimization problem in our model is based onRiddick and Whited(2009).  To the best of
8:229:16518:23:24:72:540:602:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:our knowledge, our stylized model provides one of the first dynamic corporate finance models
8:230:16610:24:24:72:540:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that explicitly allows for the presence of various selection mechanisms and is qualitatively
8:231:16702:24:24:72:411:554:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:consistent with the stylized facts we document in Figures1 and2.
8:232:16766:24:24:89:540:530:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Heckman(1979) highlighted how ignoring sample selection can lead to biased estimates.
8:233:16851:24:24:71:539:506:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In our model, the standard decreasing returns-to-scale assumption in combination with the
8:234:16940:24:24:71:539:482:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:entry of less profitable firms over time is sufficient to generate higher cash–to–assets ratios and
8:235:17039:24:24:71:539:458:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:higher sales-growth volatility.  Empirical estimates that do not control for sample selection
8:236:17132:24:24:71:539:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:may incorrectly infer that the underlying cash–flow process has become more volatile.  Put
8:237:17222:24:24:71:539:410:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:differently, those estimates could assign too much importance to increased uncertainty when
8:238:17313:24:24:71:539:386:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:B:in fact selection contributed to the rise in measured cash-flow volatility and cash holdings.6
8:239:17407:24:23:89:539:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In this paper, we argue that selection is a key driver for the secular increase in the cash-
8:240:17499:23:24:71:539:339:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to-assets ratio.  We are not the first to point out that newly listed firms in R&D–intensive
8:241:17591:24:24:71:539:315:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:industries appear to play a role.7Bates, Kahle, and Stulz(2009) find that high–tech, non-
8:242:17680:24:24:71:539:291:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dividend payers and recently listed firms have successively higher cash ratios, but they also
8:243:17773:24:24:71:539:267:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:find an increase in the non-high–tech sectors.8Booth and Zhou(2013) present evidence that
8:244:17862:24:24:71:539:243:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the  increase  in  the  average  cash–to–assets  ratio  is  due  to  changing  firm  characteristics  of
8:245:17966:24:24:71:540:219:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:high-tech firms that went public after 1980.  In concurrent work,Graham and Leary(2016)
8:246:18053:24:24:71:539:195:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:study  the  determinants  of  cash  policies  using  data  from  the  1920s  onward  to  investigate
8:247:18153:24:24:71:539:171:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:what factors were most important for cash holdings over different periods.  Related to the
8:248:18243:24:18:71:539:147:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:period we study, they also find that average cash holdings began to rise in about 1980 even
8:249:18334:18:15:85:539:129:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:6Roberts  and  Whited  (2013)  provide  a  survey  of  potential  endogeneity  issues  in  empirical  corporate
8:250:18445:15:8:72:105:114:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:finance.
8:251:18453:8:16:85:540:106:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:7Several papers find a positive relationship between cash and R&D expenditures (e.g.,Opler and Titman
8:252:18554:16:12:72:539:90:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:(1994),Opler, Pinkowitz, Stulz, and Williamson(1999),Brown and Petersen(2011),Falato and Sim(2014),
8:253:18653:12:8:72:540:78:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:He and Wintoki(2014),Lyandres and Palazzo(2015), andMalamud and Zucchi(2016) among many others).
8:254:18749:8:0:85:299:70:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:8We discuss this difference in section3.2and3.3.
9:255:18798:0:24:72:540:721:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:though within-firm cash balances declined over this period.  They also attribute the post-
9:256:18888:24:24:72:540:697:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:1980 rise in average cash balances to changes in sample composition due to new health and
9:257:18977:24:24:72:378:673:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:B:tech NASDAQ firms going public with large cash balances.9
9:258:19034:24:24:89:539:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We expand on these insights by (1) proposing an empirical measure of the selection effect,
9:259:19124:24:23:72:540:625:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(2) providing evidence for the two sample-selection mechanisms advanced by the model, and
9:260:19213:23:24:72:540:602:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(3)  highlighting  the  importance  of  the  turnover  ratio  (sales  over  assets)  as  an  important
9:261:19315:24:24:72:529:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:determinant of cash holdings at entry and therefore the secular increase in cash holdings.
9:262:19405:24:24:89:539:554:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The paper is organized as follows.  We present the model in Section 2.  The results of the
9:263:19495:24:24:72:539:530:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:empirical analysis are in Section3.  We first empirically assess the contribution of sample
9:264:19586:24:24:72:539:506:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:selection to the secular increase in cash holdings.  Then, in Section3.4, we explicitly study

9:268:19867:54:36:72:540:380:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:2    Selection and average cash holdings:  insights from a
9:269:19925:36:36:101:271:344:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:firm industry model
9:270:19944:36:24:89:539:308:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In this section, we develop a stylized heterogeneous firm industry model to illustrate how
9:271:20034:24:24:72:540:284:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:changes in the selection process can be a major driver of the average cash-to-assets ratio over
9:272:20129:24:24:72:540:260:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:time.  We assume firms belong to one of two sectors labeled as the new-economy sector and
9:273:20218:24:24:72:540:236:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:old-economy sector.  We set up the firm problem similarly toRiddick and Whited(2009).
9:274:20303:24:24:72:540:212:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:That is,  firms use a decreasing returns-to-scale technology with capital as the only input.
9:275:20395:24:24:72:540:188:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Firms can finance themselves with equity or with internal funds.  We assume a time-invariant
9:276:20487:24:23:72:540:164:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mass of potential firms exists that endogenously decides to become public (i.e., entry in the
9:277:20580:23:24:72:515:141:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:stock market).  These potential entrants are either new-economy or old-economy firms.
9:278:20665:24:24:89:539:117:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:To highlight the effect of the entry margin, both firm types are modeled identically.  That
9:279:20756:24:18:72:540:93:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is, we assume firms in both sectors share the same production technology and have the same
9:280:20846:18:16:85:539:75:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:9Seventy percent of the R&D–intensive entrants in our sample are listed on NASDAQ, while 20% are
9:281:20942:16:0:72:294:59:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:listed on the NYSE, and the remainder on AMEX.
10:282:20989:0:24:72:540:721:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:financing opportunities.  The only difference between these sectors is that, contrary to old-
10:283:21082:24:24:72:540:697:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:economy firms, new-economy firms experience a change in the conditions that influence their

12:364:24667:47:31:72:530:568:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:2.3    The underlying mechanism:  mean reversion in productivity
12:365:24731:31:24:89:539:537:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:This  section  describes  the  tight  link  between  the  cash–to–assets  ratio  of  entrants  and
12:366:24829:24:24:72:540:513:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:their productivity state.  Before we go into more detail on this link, we first briefly sketch
12:367:24923:24:24:72:540:489:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:out the model parametrization.  The firm industry equilibrium and the solution method are
12:368:25012:24:24:72:540:465:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:described in the appendix (Section A.1).  We parametrize the model at an annual frequency
12:369:25101:24:24:72:540:441:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:using calibrated values that match key features of U.S. public firms.  The calibration strategy
12:370:25196:24:24:72:539:417:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is  laid  out  in  detail  in  SectionA.2.   To  highlight  the  role  of  selection,  we  calibrate  the
12:371:25301:24:24:72:539:393:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:parameters listed in Table1 using the period 1959-1979, that is, before a marked increase
12:372:25390:24:24:72:540:369:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the cash–to-assets ratio.  Panel A lists standard parameters that we borrowed from the
12:373:25479:24:23:72:540:345:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:literature.  Panel B reports the calibrated parameters, their value, the targeted data moment,
12:374:25573:23:24:72:540:322:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and the equivalent model moments.  Finally, Panel C reports the calibration target for the
12:375:25663:24:24:72:540:298:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:exit-rate parameterλthat has been chosen to map the age distribution in the model as close
12:376:25753:24:24:72:309:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as possible to the age distribution in the data.
12:377:25801:24:24:89:539:250:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The  policy  functions  (SectionA.3)  are  fairly  standard.   The  key  insights  from  those
12:378:25895:24:24:72:540:226:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:policy functions is the importance of precautionary financing for small firms.  Large firms
12:379:25986:24:24:72:540:202:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:have a smaller precautionary savings motive because they rely on larger expected cash flows,
12:380:26078:24:24:72:540:178:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and for this  reason,  they need to retain less  cash  when  financing constraints are binding.
12:381:26173:24:24:72:540:154:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Conversely, small firms engage in larger precautionary savings, and in doing, so they deliver
12:382:26266:24:24:72:216:130:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a larger cash-to-assets ratio.
12:383:26296:24:17:89:539:106:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:This paper stresses the importance of the entry margin, i.e.  the selection process.  The
12:384:26385:17:16:81:539:89:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:11We  follow  a  reduced-form  approach  to  model  the  going-public  decision  and  choose  not  to  model  the
12:385:26498:16:12:72:540:73:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:problem of the private firm.  The selection mechanisms that drive our results will also operate in a more
12:386:26603:12:0:72:285:61:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:realistic setup along the lines ofClementi(2002).

14:446:29103:0:0:327:328:463:3:Helvetica:3:Helvetica:F:-1-0.500.510

14:451:29127:0:121:318:411:557:3:Helvetica:3:Helvetica:F:0.5Cash-to-Assets
14:452:29144:121:12:72:540:436:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:The figure reports the characteristics at entry for a firm as a function of the entry signal.  The top left panel
14:453:29257:12:11:72:540:424:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:depicts the expected firm-level productivity, the bottom left panel the capital choice at entry, the top right
14:454:29367:11:12:72:540:413:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:panel the cash balance,  and the bottom right panel the cash balance divided by total assets (i.e.,  capital
14:455:29475:12:54:72:158:401:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:plus cash holdings).
14:456:29495:54:24:72:540:347:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:invest later (top right panel) in order to minimize future equity issuance cost.  If the signal is
14:457:29593:24:24:72:540:323:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sufficiently good, the firm decides not to save any cash.  The bottom right panel reports the
14:458:29686:24:24:72:540:299:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cash–to–assets ratio of an entering firm.  As the signal improves, the firm saves less cash and
14:459:29781:24:24:72:540:275:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:invests more, thus generating a decrease in the cash–to–assets ratio.  In sum, these policy
14:460:29872:24:24:72:540:251:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:functions highlight the importance of entrants’ productivity for the average cash–to–assets
14:461:29963:24:23:72:540:227:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ratio.  Less profitable firms with low current productivity expect high growth and therefore
14:462:30055:23:24:72:540:204:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:have a higher demand for investment in the long run.  To avoid tapping into costly external
14:463:30146:24:47:72:383:180:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:financing sources too frequently, they choose to save in cash.
14:464:30208:47:31:72:526:133:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:2.4    Changes in the selection process and average cash holdings
14:465:30273:31:24:89:539:102:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Armed with the model, we investigate how the two selection mechanisms (i.e., selecting
14:466:30359:24:24:72:540:78:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:relatively  more  new–economy  firms  versus  selecting  initially  less  profitable  new–economy
14:467:30456:24:0:72:540:54:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:firms) shape the average cash holdings’ dynamics.  The starting point is the steady state of
15:468:30550:0:24:72:540:721:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the benchmark model calibrated to data from the 1959-1979 period, where the economy is
15:469:30636:24:24:72:219:697:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:populated by identical firms.
15:470:30665:24:24:89:539:673:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The first experiment is designed to explore the effect of a structural change in the com-
15:471:30754:24:24:72:540:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:position of firms (across-industry selection mechanism) on the average cash-to-assets ratio
15:472:30845:24:23:72:540:625:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(top left panel of Figure 4).  To this end, we assume the fraction of potential entrants of type
15:473:30941:23:24:72:540:602:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:oldωchanges over a time span of 35 years so that the model replicates the compositional
15:474:31028:24:24:72:456:578:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:B:change for publicly traded firms in the data (top right panel of Figure4).12
15:475:31104:24:24:89:539:554:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:A structural change in the composition of entrants is unable to generate a secular increase
15:476:31195:24:24:71:539:530:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the average cash holdings of publicly traded firms.  The solid blue lines in the bottom
15:477:31285:24:24:71:539:506:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:panels of Figure4 show the increase in average cash holdings for new-economy firms (bottom
15:478:31375:24:24:72:540:482:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:left panel) is due to the increase in the proportion of young firms (bottom right panel).  Given
15:479:31471:24:24:72:540:458:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that exit is i.i.d., a progressively larger fraction of new-economy entrants leads to an increase
15:480:31568:24:24:72:540:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the proportion of young new-economy firms.  These firms are smaller and have, on average,
15:481:31660:24:24:72:432:410:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:larger cash-to-assets ratios relative to their more mature counterparts.
15:482:31732:24:24:89:539:386:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:This  positive  effect  on  average  cash  holdings  is  counterbalanced  by  the  dynamics  of
15:483:31827:24:23:72:540:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cash holdings for old-economy firms,  as illustrated by the dashed red lines in the bottom
15:484:31917:23:24:72:540:339:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:panels of Figure4.  Because old economy firms enter in a smaller number, their composition
15:485:32007:24:24:72:540:315:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:shifts  toward  more  mature  firms  that  have,  on  average,  lower  cash-to-assets  ratios.   This
15:486:32108:24:24:72:540:291:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:effects leads to an initial decrease of average cash holdings.  It follows that the cash-holdings
15:487:32205:24:24:72:540:267:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dynamics in the two sectors offset each other, thus leaving the overall cash-to-assets ratio
15:488:32297:24:24:72:540:243:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:unchanged over time, as described by the top left panel of Figure4.  Without a change in
15:489:32385:24:24:72:540:219:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the characteristics at entry of new-economy firms, the model cannot generate an increase in
15:490:32476:24:24:72:186:195:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:average cash holdings.
15:491:32498:24:24:89:539:171:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Our second experiment investigates how a change in the characteristics of new-economy
15:492:32583:24:24:72:540:147:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:entrants (intra-industryselection) affects the cash–to–assets ratio.  Motivated by the changes
15:493:32677:24:17:72:540:123:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to institutional investors’ investment opportunities at the end of the 1970s discussed in the
15:494:32770:17:16:81:539:106:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:12To be precise, we assume the fraction of potential entrants of type old evolves over time according to
15:495:32874:16:12:72:539:90:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f7:F:ωt=  (ω−a1) +a1t−a2,  wheret=  1,...,35.   We  picka1anda2to  minimize  the  distance  between  the
15:496:32973:12:12:72:539:78:10:g_d0_f7:7:g_d0_f6:F:compositional change generated by the model and the one observed in the data.  The calibrated values ofa1
15:497:33078:12:0:72:446:66:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:anda2deliver a fraction of potential entrants of type old equal to 40% after 35 years.
16:498:33166:0:269:178:430:723:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Figure 4:  Increase in share of new-economy firms
16:499:33215:269:11:72:540:454:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:This figure reports the effect of an increase in the share of new-economy firms on average cash holdings.
16:500:33320:11:12:72:540:443:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:The top left (right) panel reports the evolution of average cash holdings (the fraction of new firms) over 35
16:501:33429:12:11:72:540:431:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:years.  The bottom left panel reports the average cash holdings of new-economy and old-economy firms.  The
16:502:33535:11:12:72:540:420:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:bottom right panel reports firms that have gone public in the last five years (young firms) as a fraction of
16:503:33643:12:40:72:440:408:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:the total number of firms.  This quantity is calculated separately for the two sectors.
16:504:33730:40:268:158:454:368:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Figure 5:  Reduction in entry costs for new-economy firms
16:505:33787:268:0:72:540:100:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:This figure reports the effect of a decrease in the entry cost for new-economy firms on average cash holdings.
17:506:33899:0:24:72:540:721:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:introduction, we study the response of the model to a reduction in the value of staying private
17:507:33994:24:24:72:540:697:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for new-economy firms.  We assume a reduction inVpover 35 years to mimic the dynamics
17:508:34079:24:24:71:539:673:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of  the  relative  size  of  entering  firms.13Figure  5  shows  this  change  reduces  the  threshold
17:509:34181:24:24:71:539:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:productivity level for entry.  That is, even small (top right panel) and less productive firms
17:510:34275:24:23:71:539:625:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(i.e.,  low-profitability  firms  with  higher  growth  potential)  choose  to  go  public.   Because
17:511:34376:23:24:71:539:602:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the shocks are mean reverting, lower-productivity firms anticipate higher productivity in the
17:512:34469:24:24:71:539:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:future and raise more cash relative to their assets at the IPO stage (bottom right panel). This
17:513:34564:24:24:71:539:554:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:behavior is a natural consequence of the entrants’ policy function discussed in section2.3.
17:514:34655:24:24:71:539:530:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:This selection mechanism only affects the average cash-to-assets ratio of new-economy firms
17:515:34746:24:24:71:540:506:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(bottom left panel),  thus replicating the empirical evidence in Figure2 of R&D–intensive
17:516:34835:24:24:71:539:482:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:firms entering with progressively higher cash balances.  The model can explain around 26%
17:517:34924:24:24:71:265:458:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:B:of the total change in cash holdings.14
17:518:34963:24:24:89:539:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:On its own, neither selection mechanism is quantitatively strong enough to explain the
17:519:35049:24:24:71:539:410:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:secular trend in cash holdings. However, the combination of theintra-industryselection effect
17:520:35142:24:24:71:539:386:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with theacross-industryselection effect - a purely selection-based mechanism - explains 46%
17:521:35233:24:23:71:135:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of the trend.
17:522:35246:23:24:89:539:339:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Figure6 compares the data (dashed red lines) with the data generated by a model that
17:523:35330:24:24:71:539:315:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:considers both selection mechanisms (solid blue lines).  Adding a change in composition on
17:524:35420:24:24:71:539:291:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:top of a reduction in the value of staying private for new-economy firms helps  the model
17:525:35509:24:24:71:539:267:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:along two dimensions.  The model generates both a secular increase in cash holdings for new
17:526:35600:24:24:71:539:243:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:economy firms at entry (top right panel) and a shift in the composition toward new-economy
17:527:35690:24:24:71:539:219:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:firms  (bottom  right  panel).   The  latteracross-industryselection  mechanism  increases  the
17:528:35785:24:24:71:539:195:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:number of new economy entrants that are smaller in the cross section, thus amplifying their
17:529:35876:24:18:71:539:171:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:effect  on  the  average  cash-to-assets  ratio.   This  amplification  channel  leads  to  a  steeper
17:530:35978:18:15:81:539:153:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:13We calculate the relative size using median values of size at entry for the seven cohorts during the period
17:531:36087:15:12:72:540:138:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:1979-2013.  We measure size in 2009 dollars using total sales (Compustat Item SALE). We assume the value
17:532:36191:12:12:72:539:126:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:of staying private for entrants of type new evolves over time according toVp,n,t= (Vp,n−a1) +a1t−a2, where
17:533:36297:12:12:72:539:114:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f7:F:t= 1,...,35.  We picka1anda2to minimize the distance between the relative size at entry generated by the
17:534:36401:12:8:72:248:102:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:model and the one observed in the data.
17:535:36440:8:16:81:539:94:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:14The increase in the average cash-to-assets ratio for new-economy firms leads to an overall increase from
17:536:36546:16:12:72:540:78:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:a steady-state value of 0.093 to a value of 0.133 (top left panel).  In the data, the average cash-to-assets ratio
17:537:36660:12:12:72:540:66:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:increases from a value of 0.081 in 1979 to a value of 0.235 in 2013.  Thus, the model explains around 26% of

18:539:36863:0:292:254:357:723:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Figure 6:  Combined

18:547:37533:23:24:72:121:259:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and 2013.
18:548:37542:24:24:89:540:235:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:As  in  the  data  (see  Figure1),  our  model  captures  the  mean-reverting  nature  of  the
18:549:37636:24:24:72:540:211:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cash-to-assets  ratio  and  thus  generates  the  secular  increase  purely  with  the  two  selection

18:552:37910:24:24:72:540:139:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cash–to–assets ratio has increased.  In the next subsection, we discuss additional implications
18:553:38005:24:0:72:442:115:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of sample selection that go beyond the secular increase in cash holdings.

19:568:38581:32:24:89:539:343:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In  addition  to  being  consistent  with  firms’  cash-holding  dynamics,  our  stylized  model
19:569:38677:24:24:72:540:319:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is  also  qualitatively  consistent  with  a  number  of  other  documented  trends  in  U.S.  public
19:570:38778:24:24:72:539:295:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:firms  over  the  last  35  years.   In  Table2,  we  summarize  the  additional  predictions  of  the
19:571:38880:24:23:72:540:271:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model.  As discussed above (section2.4), we target the size of new-economy firms relative to
19:572:38972:23:24:72:539:248:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:old-economy firms at entry to discipline the reduction inVP(outside option).  The model
19:573:39059:24:24:72:442:224:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:counterpart of the relative size at entry is shown in column I of Table2.
19:574:39132:24:24:89:539:200:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:First, the model predicts new-economy entrants have not only become relatively smaller
19:575:39218:24:24:72:540:176:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(column  I),  but  also  require  a  progressively  lower  profitability  signal  to  enter  the  equity
19:576:39322:24:24:72:540:152:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:market.   A  lower  signal  leads  to  a  decline  in  the  average  firm-level  productivity  (shock)
19:577:39424:24:24:72:540:128:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:at  entry  relative  to  old-economy  firms,  as  shown  in  column  II  of  Table2.   Due  to  the
19:578:39523:24:24:72:540:104:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:decreasing  returns-to-scale  assumption,  the  reduction  in  the  relative  size  of  new-economy
19:579:39622:24:24:72:540:80:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:entrants  decreases  the  relative  turnover  ratio  (i.e.,  the  sales-to-assets  ratio),  as  shown  in
19:580:39727:24:0:72:540:56:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:column III. The latter value goes from 83% for the cohort 1979-1983 to 47% for the cohort

20:592:40296:16:9:72:540:551:8:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f5:F:This table reports five-year averages calculated using the model-generated data where both selection mechanisms are in place.
20:593:40421:9:10:72:540:542:8:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f5:F:Column I reports the relative size at entry, column II reports the relative productivity shock at entry (z), Column III reports
20:594:40548:10:9:72:540:532:8:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f5:F:the  relative  turnover  ratio  at  entry,  Column  IV  reports  the  average  cash-to-assets  ratio,  and  columns  V  and  VI  report  the
20:595:40688:9:34:72:382:523:8:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f5:F:average and relative cross-sectional disperson of the sales’ growth rate, respectively.
20:596:40775:34:24:72:540:489:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:2009-2013.   In  any  model  with  a  decreasing  returns-to-scale  technology  assumption,  the
20:597:40871:24:24:72:540:465:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:turnover ratio is a proxy for firm-level productivity and profitability.  Because of this link,
20:598:40966:24:23:72:540:441:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the turnover ratio should be an important empirical determinant of the cash-to-assets ratio
20:599:41057:23:24:72:540:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:at the firm level.15These predictions are consistent with the findings in Fama and French
20:600:41146:24:24:72:540:394:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(2004), who document a steady decrease in size and profitability during the 1980–2001 period,
20:601:41239:24:24:72:263:370:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and highlight the role of new listings.
20:602:41278:24:24:89:539:346:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Second, the two selection mechanisms, in addition to generating a steady increase in the
20:603:41366:24:24:72:540:322:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cash-to-assets ratio (column IV), deliver an increase in the dispersion of the sales growth
20:604:41457:24:24:72:540:298:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rate that is qualitatively consistent with the data (column V), as we will show in Table5
20:605:41546:24:24:72:540:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in section3.16Without changing the volatility parameter for the productivity shock in the
20:606:41635:24:24:72:540:250:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model,  theintra-industryselection mechanism allows smaller firms to go public.  Because
20:607:41723:24:24:72:540:226:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of decreasing returns to scale,  smaller firms are characterized by higher and more volatile
20:608:41815:24:24:72:540:202:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:growth rates.  This feature is responsible for the steady increase in the dispersion of sales’
20:609:41909:24:23:72:540:178:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:growth  rates,  which  is  entirely  driven  by  sales  of  new  economy  firms  becoming  relatively
20:610:42010:23:19:72:216:155:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:B:more volatile (column VI).17
20:611:42038:19:12:81:438:136:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:15Notice that, given the stylized nature of the model, sales and profit do coincide.
20:612:42122:12:12:81:296:124:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:16The sales growth rate is defined in SectionA.2.
20:613:42171:12:15:81:540:112:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:17Davis  et  al.(2007)  show  how,  contrary  to  what  happened  in  the  private  sector,  the  cross-sectional
20:614:42284:15:12:72:540:97:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:dispersion of firm growth rates for publicly listed U.S. companies has increased over the 1978–2004 period.
20:615:42391:12:12:72:539:85:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:Brown  and  Kapadia(2007)  show  the  increase  in  firm-specific  risk  is  a  direct  result  of  riskier  firms  going
20:616:42512:12:0:72:250:73:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:public, hinting at a selection mechanism.
21:617:42555:0:24:89:539:721:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:To sum up, our model suggests that any data analysis should pay attention to entry de-
21:618:42641:24:24:72:540:697:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cisions of firms, particularly when a specific firm type (here R&D–intensive firms) becomes
21:619:42732:24:24:72:540:673:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:increasingly dominant in the sample.  Inference based on exogenous changes in deep param-
21:620:42821:24:24:72:540:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:eters (e.g., an increase in the cash–flow volatility parameter over time) can be confounded
21:621:42912:24:23:72:540:625:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with factors that are outside the firm’s optimization problem, but are due to changes in the
21:622:43004:23:24:72:540:602:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:selection process into the stock market.  For example, empirical estimates could assign too
21:623:43095:24:24:72:540:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:much importance to increased uncertainty when in fact selection contributes to the rise in
21:624:43185:24:55:72:266:554:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cash-flow volatility and cash holdings.
21:625:43224:55:35:72:527:499:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:3    The empirical evidence on sample selection effects
21:626:43279:35:24:89:539:464:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In  this  section,  we  explore  the  model’s  predictions  by  studying  how  sample  selection
21:627:43375:24:24:72:540:440:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:affects  the  secular  increase  in  the  cash–to–assets  ratio.   The  data  corroborate  what  the
21:628:43475:24:24:72:540:416:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model suggests:  most of the action for the change in the cash–to–assets ratio is at the entry
21:629:43569:24:24:72:540:392:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:margin and is driven by an increasing share of smaller and less profitable R&D–intensive
21:630:43657:24:24:72:483:368:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:firms with higher cash-to-assets ratios that went public during the last 35 years.
21:631:43739:24:24:89:539:344:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We first describe the data set and definitions.  Then we show a negative time trend exists
21:632:43829:24:24:72:540:320:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the cash–to–assets ratio at the firm level, whereas pooled OLS regressions show a positive
21:633:43922:24:24:72:540:296:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:time trend.  A negative firm-level trend together with a positive trend in the cross-section
21:634:44014:24:23:72:540:272:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:suggests the secular increase in cash is mainly a byproduct of sample selection. We isolate the
21:635:44109:23:24:72:540:249:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:effect of sample selection on the positive time trend using a simple accounting decomposition
21:636:44202:24:24:72:540:225:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and show that newly listed R&D–intensive firms are responsible for the bulk in the increase
21:637:44293:24:24:72:540:201:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of  the  average  cash-to-assets  ratio.18We  conclude  our  analysis  by  providing  evidence  for
21:638:44392:24:24:72:540:177:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the two selection mechanisms discussed in the model and by studying the determinants of
21:639:44479:24:18:72:369:153:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:R&D–intensive firms’ cash holdings before they go public.
21:640:44536:18:16:81:539:135:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:18We rule out firm exit as a driver of the secular increase in the cash–to–assets ratio (see figure12in the
21:641:44643:16:11:71:539:119:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:appendix).   We  find  the  average  cash–to–assets  ratio  at  exit  is  close  to  the  cross-sectional  average  of  the
21:642:44766:11:0:71:373:108:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:cash–to–assets ratio.  This behavior is consistent with exit being i.i.d.
22:643:44841:0:32:72:412:721:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:3.1    R&D–intensive firms:  Data and definitions
22:644:44890:32:23:89:539:689:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We use annual Compustat data for the period 1959-2013, excluding financial firms (SIC
22:645:44975:23:24:72:540:666:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:codes 6000 to 6999) and regulated industries (SIC codes 4000 to 4999), non-U.S.-incorporated
22:646:45067:24:24:72:534:642:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:firms, and those not traded on the three major exchanges:  NYSE, AMEX, and NASDAQ.
22:647:45149:24:24:89:539:618:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:R&D–intensive  firms  are  firms  that  belong  to  an  industry  (using  the  three-level-digit
22:648:45245:24:24:72:540:594:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f3:B:SICcode) that has an average R&D investment–to–assets ratio of at least 2%.  We choose
22:649:45331:24:24:72:540:570:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:2% as the cut-off level because it is the minimum R&D–to–asset ratios of the top quintile
22:650:45420:24:24:72:270:546:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:B:industries in terms of R&D to assets.19
22:651:45459:24:24:89:539:522:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Our  R&D–based  industry  classification  is  consistent  with  other  classifications  used  in
22:652:45555:24:24:72:540:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:previous empirical studies.  The seven industries that account for the bulk of R&D–intensive
22:653:45647:24:24:72:539:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:entrants are the same industriesBrown et al.(2009) use to identify the high–tech sector.
22:654:45735:24:24:72:540:450:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In addition, our broadly defined R&D–intensive sector contains all the industries classified
22:655:45827:24:23:72:540:426:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as “Internet  and  Technology  Firms” byLoughran and Ritter(2004), with the exception of
22:656:45915:23:24:72:540:403:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Telephone Equipment (SIC 481), which we exclude by construction because it belongs to a
22:657:46002:24:24:72:176:379:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:B:regulated industry.20
22:658:46023:24:24:89:539:355:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We want to follow the dynamics of an entering cohort.  To this end, we sort firms into
22:659:46109:24:24:72:540:331:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:seven  cohorts  using  non-overlapping  periods  of  five  years  starting  with  the  window  1979-
22:660:46209:24:24:72:540:307:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:1983.  A cohort definition based on a five-year window is fairly standard in the firm-dynamics
22:661:46303:24:24:72:540:283:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:literature but not essential to our results.  We define anentrantas a firm that reports a
22:662:46392:24:97:72:457:259:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:B:fiscal year-end value of the stock price for the first time (itemPRCCF).21
22:663:46466:97:15:81:539:162:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:19We obtain very similar results if we narrow our definition down to using the seven specific industries
22:664:46570:15:12:72:540:147:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:that account for the bulk of R&D–intensive entrants:  Computer and Data Processing Services (SIC737,
22:665:46670:12:12:72:539:135:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:26% of total entrants), Drugs (SIC283, 15%), Medical Instruments and Supplies (SIC384, 9%), Electronic
22:666:46772:12:12:72:540:123:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:Components and Accessories (SIC367, 8%), Computer and Office Equipment (SIC357, 7%), Measuring
22:667:46866:12:9:71:465:111:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:and Controlling Devices (SIC382, 5%), and Communications Equipment (SIC366, 5%).
22:668:46946:9:15:81:540:102:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:20Differently  fromBates  et  al.(2009),  we  do  not  to  follow  the  classification  inLoughran  and  Ritter
22:669:47057:15:12:71:539:87:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:(2004), because it excludes one of the most relevant R&D–intensive industries (Drugs,SIC283) from the
22:670:47158:12:8:72:169:75:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:R&D–intensive sector.
22:671:47179:8:16:81:540:67:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:21Our results are robust to using value-weighted data (e.g., Table11in the Appendix) or defining entry
22:672:47281:16:0:71:506:51:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:based on the IPO dates provided by Jay Ritter.http://bear.warrington.ufl.edu/ritter/ipodata.htm.
24:673:49468:0:32:72:335:721:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:3.2    The time trend in cash holdings
24:674:49506:32:23:89:539:689:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The model presented in Section 2 is able to generate a positive trend in cash holdings
24:675:49592:23:24:72:540:666:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:despite the mean-reverting nature of the cash-to-assets ratio at the firm level, which means
24:676:49684:24:24:72:540:642:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that new entrants deplete cash at a lower rate than the rate at which they increase cash at
24:677:49775:24:24:72:539:618:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:entry, as illustrated in Figure7.  In this section, we provide evidence for this selection-based
24:678:49871:24:24:72:135:594:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:explanation.
24:679:49883:24:24:89:539:570:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We first estimate the time trend in the cash–to–assets ratio using all firms over the period
24:680:49975:24:24:72:540:546:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:1979–2013.  The resulting trend is positive:  cash holdings represented around 11% of total
24:681:50066:24:24:72:540:522:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:assets  for  the  typical  firm  in  1979,  and  they  have  increased  by  14%  over  the  subsequent
24:682:50168:24:24:72:540:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:35  years  (column  I  of  Table3).   Column  II  of  Table3  shows  the  differences  in  the  time
24:683:50268:24:24:72:540:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:trend across sectors by including a dummy variable that takes a value of zero if a firm is
24:684:50358:24:24:72:540:450:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:non-R&D–intensive, and 1 otherwise.  The estimated slope for the R&D sector is one order
24:685:50446:24:23:72:540:426:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of magnitude larger than the estimated slope for the non-R&D sector (66 b.p.  vs.  5.5 b.p.).
24:686:50539:23:24:72:540:403:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The implied increase in cash holdings for the non–R&D sector over the 35-year period is very
24:687:50631:24:24:72:540:379:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:small (around 2%), while cash holdings in the R&D sector surged from an average value of
24:688:50719:24:24:72:540:355:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:14% in 1979 to an average value of 35% in 2013.  The secular increase in the cash-to-assets
24:689:50810:24:24:72:540:331:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ratio appears to be a phenomenon that pertains almost exclusively to the R&D–intensive
24:690:50896:24:24:72:105:307:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sector.
24:691:50903:24:24:89:539:283:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Pooled OLS regressions allow us to identify R&D–intensive firms as the driver of the sec-
24:692:50992:24:24:72:540:259:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ular increase in cash holdings.  However, the cash–to–assets ratio is fairly persistent (see also
24:693:51089:24:24:72:539:235:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Figure13andLemmon et al.(2008)), and pooled OLS regressions are not conclusive with
24:694:51172:24:24:71:539:211:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:regard to each firm’s individual cash–to–assets evolution.  In fact, incumbent R&D–intensive
24:695:51264:24:24:71:539:187:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:firms  could  have  indeed  increased  their  cash–to–assets  ratios  over  time.   To  address  the
24:696:51364:24:23:71:539:163:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:persistence issue, we perform firm–by–firm regressions and report average values of the esti-
24:697:51457:23:24:71:539:140:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mated coefficients.  We set the time variable equal to zero the first year the firm appears in
24:698:51551:24:24:71:539:116:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the sample.  In this way, we control for the cash holdings at entry at the firm level.  The re-
24:699:51646:24:24:71:539:92:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sults show a negative change in average cash holdings for incumbents.  The estimated yearly
24:700:51737:24:0:71:539:68:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:within-firm change in average cash holdings over 35 years is -50 b.p.  (column III). Column
25:701:51830:0:24:72:540:721:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:IV shows that R&D–intensive firms start with much larger cash balances and deplete cash
25:702:51917:24:24:72:264:697:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:faster than non-R&D–intensive firms.

25:704:52042:24:24:72:539:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the 1979–2013 period.  In the remaining columns of Table3,  we estimate the time-trend-
25:705:52129:24:23:72:540:625:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:by-age category because firms might not be at theirsteady-statecash level shortly after the
25:706:52220:23:24:72:540:602:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:IPO. In particular,  we defineyoung  firmsas firms that have been public for at most five

25:710:52591:24:24:72:540:506:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:firms deplete cash faster than mature firms, and (iii) the estimated slope for R&D–intensive

27:828:57399:46:32:72:421:238:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:3.4    Controlling for selection:  empirical evidence
27:829:57452:32:23:89:539:206:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:So far, our empirical evidence shows the importance of newly listed firms for the secular

27:833:57814:24:24:72:131:111:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:predictions.
27:834:57826:24:24:89:539:87:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The model predicts that a change in the composition at entry plays no role in shaping the

31:965:66619:24:24:72:392:428:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with other important determinants of corporate cash holdings.

31:967:66768:24:24:72:540:380:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the IPO year. For both sectors, average cash holdings are smaller before the IPO year and de-
31:968:66861:24:24:72:540:356:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:crease the year after the IPO below their pre–IPO values.26However, only the R&D–intensive
31:969:66951:24:24:71:539:332:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sector (left panel) shows a secular trend in average cash holdings before the IPO year, a phe-
31:970:67045:24:24:71:469:308:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:nomenon that clearly does not depend on a higher retention of IPO proceeds.

31:973:67296:24:24:72:539:237:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the cash holding literature (e.g.,Azar et al.(2016) andBates et al.(2009)) and include the
31:974:67386:24:24:71:539:213:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:turnover ratio as a proxy for the underlying total revenue productivity shock, as suggested
31:975:67477:24:24:71:539:189:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:by the model.  In column I, we consider all variables.  Only the T-bill rate does not enter

34:1053:71641:17:12:72:540:478:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:This table reports time-series regressions where the dependent variable is the change in the average cash-
34:1054:71747:12:12:72:540:466:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:to-assets ratio before IPO over the period 1979-2013.  We only consider firms in the R&D-intensive sector.

34:1056:71958:12:12:72:540:442:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:definitions can be found in Table 6.  We report robust standard errors.  * denotes significance at the 10%
34:1057:72064:12:54:72:465:430:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:level, ** denotes significance at the 5% level, and *** denotes significance at the 1% level.
34:1058:72157:54:24:89:539:376:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:All  of  the  key  variables  identified  in  Table6  have  a  pronounced  time  trend  over  the
34:1059:72254:24:24:72:540:352:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:period 1979-2013.  In Table7, we address the problem of having spurious correlations due
34:1060:72342:24:24:72:540:328:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to common time trends by regressing the change in entrants’ average cash–to–assets ratio
34:1061:72430:24:24:72:540:304:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on the change in the average values of the turnover ratio, R&D–to-assets ratio, net working
34:1062:72521:24:24:72:247:280:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:capital, and leverage, respectively.
34:1063:72557:24:24:89:539:256:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Our results show the change in the average turnover ratio alone explains more than half of
34:1064:72647:24:23:72:540:232:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the variation in the average cash-to-assets ratio’s fluctuations at entry over the period 1979-
34:1065:72742:23:24:72:540:209:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:2013 (column I). The other variables have a much smaller individual explanatory power, with
34:1066:72833:24:24:72:540:185:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the only exception of leverage that can individually explain around 20% of the variation in
34:1067:72924:24:24:72:540:161:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the change in the average cash-to-assets ratio at entry (column V). In column VI, we consider
34:1068:73017:24:24:72:540:137:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the joint explanatory power of all the variables.  As we can see, only the turnover ratio and
34:1069:73110:24:24:72:540:113:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:leverage  come  out  significant  and  the  model  explains  62%  of  the  variation  in  the  data,  a
34:1070:73213:24:24:72:540:89:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:small improvement over the model that only considers the turnover ratio.  This last exercise
34:1071:73305:24:0:72:540:65:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:provides additional evidence on the importance of the turnover ratio in shaping the dynamics
35:1072:73399:0:54:72:361:721:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of the average cash-to-assets ratio over the last 35 years.
35:1073:73458:54:36:72:194:667:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:4    Conclusion
35:1074:73473:36:24:89:539:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:This paper finds that sample selection has been a key driver of the increase in the average
35:1075:73564:24:24:72:540:607:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cash–to–assets ratio for U.S. public companies over the last 35 years.  While new entrants to
35:1076:73657:24:24:72:540:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the stock market have increased their cash–to–assets ratios, the typical U.S. public company
35:1077:73749:24:24:72:540:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:experiences a decline in cash holdings over time.  The selection effect is powerful enough to
35:1078:73842:24:23:72:446:535:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reverse the negative within-firm effect and to generate a secular increase.
35:1079:73917:23:24:89:539:512:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:A stylized firm industry model with endogenous entry allows us to study how selection
35:1080:74002:24:24:72:540:488:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mechanisms can shape the average cash–to–assets ratio. More than a shift in the composition
35:1081:74093:24:24:72:540:464:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of R&D–intensive firms, a shift toward smaller, initially less productive, but higher-growth-
35:1082:74186:24:24:72:540:440:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:potential firms is the key driver of higher cash balances at IPO. This mechanisms is backed
35:1083:74277:24:24:72:540:416:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:up  by the  data  as we  show with bootstrap  sampling  techniques.  The data also  show the
35:1084:74369:24:24:72:540:392:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:turnover ratio,  as a proxy for firm-level productivity,  is a key predictor for cash ratios at
35:1085:74464:24:24:72:220:368:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:entry, as our model suggests.
35:1086:74493:24:24:89:539:344:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:All in all, our results suggest a new direction in the debate about the causes of the secular
35:1087:74586:24:24:72:540:320:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:increase in the corporate cash–to–assets ratio and other observed changes in investment and
35:1088:74677:24:24:72:540:296:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:financing  practices.   Instead  of  focusing  on  factors  that  influence  incumbents’  investment
35:1089:74777:24:23:72:540:272:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and financing decisions, we advocate for a shift of research efforts toward understanding why
35:1090:74870:23:24:72:540:249:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:more R&D–intensive firms go public and why they do so with higher cash–to–assets ratios
35:1091:74957:24:0:72:123:225:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:over time.

42:1260:85508:0:12:467:474:360:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:}
42:1261:85509:12:24:479:539:348:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:denotes  the

42:1264:85598:44:0:176:275:247:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Γit+1(W′) = (1−φ)
42:1265:85615:0:22:276:282:261:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:∫

42:1267:85617:0:22:290:296:261:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:∫
42:1268:85618:22:0:296:321:239:8:g_d0_f11:8:g_d0_f5:F:Bi(W)
42:1269:85623:0:44:324:464:247:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:C:dΓit(W)dF(z′|z) +εit+1(W),
42:1270:85649:44:24:101:543:203:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:whereBi(W) denotes the policy functions of incumbents andω= Γot+1(W′)/(Γnt+1(W′)+
42:1271:85730:24:32:101:154:179:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Γot+1(W′)).
42:1272:85741:32:24:71:539:147:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The distribution of firms evolves in the following way.  A mass of entrants receives a signal
42:1273:85834:24:24:71:540:123:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and some decide to enter.  The signalqdetermines the productivity level of the following
42:1274:85922:24:24:71:539:99:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:period.  Firms choose savings and capital investment.  These choices determine the expected
42:1275:86013:24:24:71:539:75:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:net  worth  for  the  following  period.   Conditional  on  not  exiting,  incumbent  firms  pick  the
42:1276:86115:24:0:71:530:51:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:period’s investment, internal, or external funds.  The shocks follow a Markov distribution.
43:1277:86208:0:32:72:227:721:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:A.2    Parametrization
43:1278:86230:32:23:89:539:689:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We parametrize the model at an annual frequency using calibrated parameters that match
43:1279:86316:23:24:72:540:666:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:key features of U.S. public companies.  To highlight the role of selection, we calibrate the
43:1280:86408:24:24:72:513:642:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:parameters using the period 1959-1979, i.e.  before the large increase in cash–holdings.
43:1281:86496:24:24:89:539:618:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:A few standard parameters are set to values used in the literature.  Following Hennessy
43:1282:86583:24:24:72:540:594:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and Whited (2007), we set the decreasing returns-to-scale parameter to 0.62 and the depreci-
43:1283:86675:24:24:72:540:570:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ation rate to 0.15.  FollowingRiddick and Whited(2009), we set the annual risk-free interest
43:1284:86767:24:24:71:539:546:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rate to 4% and the conditional standard deviation of the idiosyncratic shock to 0.121.  Table
43:1285:86860:24:24:71:321:522:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:1 reports the parameter values and their targets.
43:1286:86909:24:24:89:539:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We calibrate the remaining parameters to match key moments, using data from the period
43:1287:86995:24:24:71:540:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:1959–1979.  The proportion of potential entrants of type old (ω) is set to 0.668.  This value
43:1288:87088:24:24:71:539:450:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:allows us to replicate the composition of publicly traded firms during the period 1959-1979.
43:1289:87180:24:23:71:540:426:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We set the persistence parameter equal to 0.90 – a value within the estimates provided by
43:1290:87269:23:24:71:539:403:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Hennessy and Whited(2007) – to match the standard deviation of the sales’ growth rate
43:1291:87354:24:24:71:494:379:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:during the period 1959-1979.  We define the latter quantity as ∆yt=yt−yt−10.5yt−1+0.5yt−1.
43:1292:87444:24:24:89:539:355:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Then we calibrate a set of parameters to replicate key cash holdings moments for publicly
43:1293:87533:24:24:72:540:331:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:traded firms in 1979.  First, we calibrate the cost of carrying cash inside the firm,ν, to match
43:1294:87629:24:24:72:540:307:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the average cash–to–assets ratio.  Second, we choose a number for the value of staying private
43:1295:87723:24:24:72:540:283:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to match the average cash–to–assets ratio at entry.  The proportional equity issuance cost
43:1296:87813:24:24:72:540:259:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(κ) is set to match the average equity-to-assets ratio over the period 1959-1979.  We define
43:1297:87905:24:24:72:540:235:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the cash–to–assets ratio in the model as cash holdings divided by the beginning of the period
43:1298:87998:24:24:72:540:211:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:capital plus cash holdings, whereas the equity–to–assets ratio as equity issuance divided by
43:1299:88090:24:24:72:351:187:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the beginning of the period capital plus cash holdings.
43:1300:88145:24:23:89:542:163:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The parameter that governs the investment adjustment cost is set to deliver an investment-
43:1301:88235:23:24:72:516:140:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:B:rate standard deviation close to the one found in the data over the period 1959-1979.28
43:1302:88322:24:24:89:539:116:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The parameter that governs the shape of the Pareto distribution,ξ, over the set of signals
43:1303:88412:24:18:72:540:92:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is chosen to match the size of entrants relative to the size of incumbents of age 5.  We measure
43:1304:88508:18:16:81:540:74:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:28We measure the investment rate in the data as capital expenditures (Compustat itemcapx) divided by
43:1305:88608:16:0:72:411:58:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:the previous period value of net property, plant, and equipment (itemppent).
44:1306:88686:0:24:72:539:721:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:firm size using total sales.29Panel B of Table1 reports the simulated moments together with
44:1307:88777:24:24:72:213:697:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:their empirical counterpart.
44:1308:88805:24:24:89:539:673:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:To  conclude,  we  set  the  exogenous  exit  rate  (λ)  to  7%,  a  value  that  delivers  an  age
44:1309:88904:24:24:72:540:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(i.e.,  years  since  entry)  distribution  close  to  the  age  distribution  in  Compustat  over  the
44:1310:89007:24:23:72:539:625:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:period 1979-2013 (Panel C of Table1).  In our model (as in the data), the years since entry
44:1311:89098:23:24:72:540:602:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:distribution matters because firms that recently IPOed tend to be smaller and have larger
44:1312:89187:24:24:72:540:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cash–to–assets ratios.  For this reason, we choose an exit rate that delivers an age distribution
44:1313:89284:24:47:72:233:554:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as close as possible to the data.
44:1314:89317:47:31:72:130:507:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:Solution
44:1315:89325:31:24:89:539:476:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We solve the incumbent problem by value function iteration.  We discretize the firm-level
44:1316:89414:24:24:72:540:452:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:shock with 35 grid points using the method inRouwenhorst(1995).  We discretize the capital
44:1317:89504:24:24:72:540:428:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:grid using 200 grid points, the net leverage grid for old-economy firms using 100 grid points,
44:1318:89598:24:24:72:540:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and the cash grid for new-economy firms using 100 grid points.  We also scale the revenue
44:1319:89687:24:24:72:364:380:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:function so that the capital choice is between zero and 1.
44:1320:89745:24:24:89:539:356:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We also solve the entrant problem by value function iteration.  We discretize the signal
44:1321:89833:24:24:72:540:332:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:space using 100 grid points.  The lower (upper) bound of the signal grid coincides with the
44:1322:89924:24:24:72:540:308:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:lower (upper) bound of the firm-level shock grid.  We use a discrete version of the Pareto
44:1323:90014:24:46:72:460:284:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:distribution to allocate the mass of potential entrants over the signal space.
44:1324:90092:46:32:72:306:238:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:A.3    Incumbent policy functions
44:1325:90125:32:24:89:540:206:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Figure10illustrates  the  policy  functions  for  an  incumbent  firm  as  a  function  of  the
44:1326:90220:24:23:72:540:182:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:firm–level  shock.   The  top  panels  are  policies  for  two  firms  that  have  the  same  size,  as
44:1327:90323:23:24:72:540:159:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:measured by their beginning of the period capital, and only differ in their beginning of the
44:1328:90415:24:24:72:540:135:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:period  cash  balances.   The  left  panel  shows  these  two  firms  choose  the  same  capital  next
44:1329:90517:24:24:72:540:111:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:period  if  they  are  both  distributing  dividends  or  issuing  equity.   For  small  values  of  the
44:1330:90621:24:18:72:540:87:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:shock, both firms have the same investment and financing policies.  In particular, when the
44:1331:90712:18:16:81:539:69:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:29We assumeQ(q) = 1−(q/q)ξ,ξ >1, where qis the lower bound of the signal grid.  For further details,
44:1332:90812:16:0:72:283:53:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:see Appendix B inClementi and Palazzo(2016).
