45:1393:91727:12:53:72:327:296:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:considering the same level of beginning-of-the-period cash.
45:1394:91786:53:24:72:540:243:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:productivity shock is very low,  both firms find it more convenient to distribute dividends
45:1395:91877:24:24:72:540:219:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rather than to invest.  As the productivity increases (i.e., the shock becomes larger), in order
45:1396:91973:24:24:72:540:195:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to take advantage of a good state, both firms decide to reduce their dividend distributions
45:1397:92064:24:24:72:540:171:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and to invest more.  If the shock becomes large enough, firms save precautionarily.  Because
45:1398:92156:24:24:72:540:147:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:issuing equity is costly, firms save internal resources to avoid equity issues in the near future;
45:1399:92254:24:24:72:540:123:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that is,  they seek a reduction in their external financing costs.  If the shock is very large,
45:1400:92349:24:24:72:540:99:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:it  becomes  optimal  to  stop  saving  and  to  issue  equity  to  finance  a  larger  investment.   In
45:1401:92453:24:24:72:540:75:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the latter case, both firms have similar investment policies, but the firm with less cash has
45:1402:92546:24:0:72:540:51:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to issue more costly equity and invest slightly less compared to the firm with larger cash
46:1403:92638:0:24:72:540:721:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:holdings.  The difference in equity issuance is exactly equal to the cash balance differential
46:1404:92732:24:24:72:540:697:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:multiplied by 1 +κ(i.e.  1+ equity issuance cost).  To summarize, the three panels show that
46:1405:92824:24:24:72:540:673:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cash-rich firms have a larger amount of internal resources that allows them to (i) distribute
46:1406:92917:24:24:72:540:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:more dividends when they are financially unconstrained, (ii) invest more and save more when
46:1407:93008:24:23:72:540:625:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:financing constraints are binding, and (iii) reduce their financing cost when they decide to
46:1408:93100:23:24:72:434:602:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:invest in excess of their internal resources, everything else being equal.
46:1409:93174:24:24:89:539:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Capital is an endogenous state variable because of capital adjustment costs.  The bottom
46:1410:93262:24:24:72:540:554:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:panels  of  Figure  10  show  the  policies  for  two  firms  that  only  differ  in  their  beginning-of-
46:1411:93368:24:24:72:540:530:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:period capital stock (i.e., size). The patterns of the investment and financing policies are very
46:1412:93465:24:24:72:540:506:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:similar to the ones in the top panels.  What emerges from these patterns is the importance
46:1413:93555:24:24:72:540:482:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of precautionary financing for small firms.  The bottom panels show that large firms have
46:1414:93644:24:24:72:540:458:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a  smaller  precautionary  savings  motive  because  they  rely  on  larger  expected  cash  flows,
46:1415:93743:24:24:72:540:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and  for  this  reason  they  need  to  retain  less  cash  when  financing  constraints  are  binding.
46:1416:93846:24:24:72:540:410:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Conversely, small firms engage in larger precautionary savings, and in doing so they deliver
46:1417:93938:24:24:72:540:386:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a larger cash-to-assets ratio given (i) their larger amount of savings and (ii) their smaller
46:1418:94031:24:46:72:233:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:beginning-of-the-period capital.
46:1419:94063:46:32:72:148:316:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:Simulation
46:1420:94073:32:23:89:539:284:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We simulate a panel of 40,000 firms for 300 periods to let the economy settle in the ergodic
46:1421:94165:23:24:72:540:261:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:state.  At each timet, a fractionλof firms exits the economy.  These firms are replaced by
46:1422:94255:24:24:72:540:237:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:an equal mass of entrants in each period.  We discard the first 100 periods and calibrate the
46:1423:94348:24:24:72:233:213:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model using the remaining 200.
46:1424:94378:24:24:89:539:189:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:To  run  our  experiments,  we  start  from  the  stationary  distribution  and  simulate  our
46:1425:94472:24:24:72:540:165:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:economy for an additional 35 years.  We repeat the simulation 200 times and report average
46:1426:94562:24:0:72:244:141:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:values across the 200 simulations.
47:1427:94598:0:36:72:377:721:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:B    Supplemental Empirical Results
47:1428:94633:36:24:89:539:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In this appendix, we provide graphs and tables to supplement the empirical analysis in
47:1429:94719:24:40:72:498:661:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the main body of the paper.  All figures and tables are at the end of the document.
47:1430:94802:40:24:72:540:621:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:B:The secular increase in cash.Figure 11 shows the average cash–to–assets ratio for U.S.
47:1431:94888:24:24:72:540:597:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f4:B:public companies over the period 1958–2013.  What has been dubbed asthe secular increase
47:1432:94976:24:24:72:540:573:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(Bates et al. (2009)) starts in 1979.  In the period 1979–2013, the average cash-holdings value
47:1433:95071:24:41:72:270:549:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:goes from 0.08 in 1979 to 0.25 in 2013.
47:1434:95110:41:24:72:540:508:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:B:Which Cohorts Drove up the Cash–to–Assets Ratio?Given the persistence of cash
47:1435:95187:24:24:72:539:484:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:balances documented in Table3, we followBrown and Kapadia(2007) and estimate a model
47:1436:95271:24:23:72:540:460:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that includes a cohort fixed effect using firms that become public from 1959 onward.  The
47:1437:95360:23:24:72:230:437:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:results are reported in Table9.
47:1438:95391:24:24:89:539:413:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:When we include cohort fixed effects, the positive trend in column I becomes not signifi-
47:1439:95480:24:24:72:540:389:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cant.  In column II, the estimates of the cohort fixed effects are differences from the excluded
47:1440:95576:24:24:72:540:365:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cohort (1974–1978), whose estimated value is given by the intercept.  Column II makes clear
47:1441:95667:24:24:72:540:341:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that no differences exist in cohort fixed effects prior to the 1979-1983 cohort, whereas starting
47:1442:95764:24:24:72:540:317:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with the latter cohort, the fixed effect becomes significantly bigger and its evolution mimics
47:1443:95858:24:24:72:540:293:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the evolution of the average cash holdings at entry depicted in Figure1.  In columns III and
47:1444:95950:24:24:72:540:269:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:IV, we separately estimate cohort fixed effects for R&D–intensive and non–R&D–intensive
47:1445:96037:24:24:72:540:245:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:firms. In both cases, no significant differences exist in cohort fixed effects among the first four
47:1446:96136:24:24:72:540:221:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cohorts, thus supporting the evidence in Figure2 that places the beginning of the secular
47:1447:96225:24:23:72:341:197:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:increase in cash holdings with the 1979–1983 cohort.
47:1448:96277:23:24:89:539:174:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:By contrast, starting with the excluded cohort, the cohort fixed effects are always sig-
47:1449:96365:24:24:72:540:150:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:nificantly different from the excluded cohort (the intercept) for the R&D–intensive sector.
47:1450:96456:24:24:72:540:126:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In addition, starting with the 1984-1988 cohort and up to 1999-2003 cohort the fixed effect
47:1451:96547:24:24:72:540:102:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:becomes  significantly  larger  (i.e.,  the  difference  in  the  fixed  effect  between  two  successive
47:1452:96652:24:24:72:358:78:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cohorts is positive and significantly different from zero).
47:1453:96711:24:0:89:539:54:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:On the other hand, the cohort fixed effects for the non–R&D–intensive sector (column
48:1454:96797:0:24:72:540:721:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:II) are significantly different from the 1974-1978 cohort only for the 1999–2003 cohort.30Dif-
48:1455:96891:24:24:71:539:697:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ferently from the R&D–intensive sector, only the 1984-1988 cohort fixed effect (significantly
48:1456:96984:24:24:71:539:673:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:smaller) and 1999–2003 cohort fixed effect (significantly larger) are statistically different from
48:1457:97082:24:24:71:539:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the 1979-1983 cohort fixed effect.  In addition, the magnitude of the cohort fixed effects is
48:1458:97175:24:23:71:539:625:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:always much smaller for the non–R&D–intensive sector, furthering the evidence of a minor
48:1459:97263:23:41:71:471:602:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:role played by this sector in determining the secular increase in cash holdings.
48:1460:97343:41:24:71:540:561:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:B:Cash  decomposition:  Selection  effect  versus  within  effect.Table  10  reports  the
48:1461:97430:24:24:71:539:537:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:contribution of theselection effectand of thewithin changeon a year–by–year basis for the

48:1463:97607:24:24:71:539:489:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:average cash holdings due to incumbents (within  change) and the change in average cash

48:1465:97790:24:24:71:539:441:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:generated by R&D–intensive firms and the selection effect generated by non-R&D–intensive
48:1466:97878:24:23:71:539:417:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:firms.31The  average  cash  holdings  equal 0.082  in 1979 and  0.237 in 2012,  an  increase  of
48:1467:97974:23:24:71:540:394:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:0.152.  We can decompose the actual increase in the contribution of thewithin  changeand

48:1469:98152:24:41:71:350:346:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the overall contribution of theselection effectis 0.343.

48:1490:98627:49:16:81:539:141:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:30During the first half of the 2000s, two events had a significant impact on corporate cash holdings:  the
48:1491:98733:16:12:72:540:125:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:Sarbanes–Oxley Act and the 2003 dividend tax cut.Bargeron et al.(2010) document a significant increase

48:1493:98936:12:8:71:352:101:10:g_d0_f7:10:g_d0_f7:F:increase in cash holdings in anticipation of the dividend tax cut.
48:1494:99002:8:0:81:435:93:7:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f7:F:31Table11below shows the results are even robust to value-weighted cash ratios.
49:1495:99083:0:24:72:540:721:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:where the first term is the change in average cash holdings due to incumbents (within change),
49:1496:99177:24:24:72:539:697:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f11:B:and the second term is the change in average cash holdings due to the selection effect.It
49:1497:99266:24:24:71:540:673:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:denotes the number of incumbents in the sample between timet−1 andt,Etdenotes the
49:1498:99347:24:24:71:540:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:number of entrants in the sample at timet, andXt−1denotes the number of firms that exit
49:1499:99434:24:23:71:539:625:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the sample at the end of timet−1.  The weight is given by the value of the firm at timetover
49:1500:99526:23:24:71:539:602:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the total value of the firms in the sample at timet.  We measure the firm’s value as the sum
49:1501:99618:24:24:71:540:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of total liabilities (Compustat itemLT) and market value of equity, which is calculated as
49:1502:99708:24:24:71:540:554:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the product of the number of shares outstanding (Compustat itemCSHO) times the price
49:1503:99792:24:24:71:276:530:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:per share (Compustat itemPRCCC) .
49:1504:99825:24:24:89:539:506:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:As in the equally weighted case, R&D–intensive entrants play a key role in shaping the
49:1505:99911:24:24:72:540:482:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:time-series evolution of the value-weighted cash–to–assets ratio.  However, value weighting
49:1506:100002:24:24:72:540:458:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sheds a different light on the phenomenon itself. When we consider all the firms in the sample,
49:1507:100097:24:24:72:540:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the within effect and the selection effect due to R&D–intensive entrants have roughly the
49:1508:100186:24:24:72:540:410:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:same importance in explaining how the value-weighted cash-to-assets ratio evolves over time.
49:1509:100278:24:24:72:540:386:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:However, it is enough to eliminate the top 1% of the size distribution from the sample to
49:1510:100367:24:23:72:540:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:make the selection effect due to R&D–intensive entrants the most important driving force.
49:1511:100456:23:24:72:540:339:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:When  we  eliminate  firms  in  the  top  5%  of  the  size  distribution,  we  moreover  obtain  the
49:1512:100557:24:41:72:466:315:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:negative within-effect results, consistent with the equally weighted approach.
49:1513:100635:41:24:72:539:274:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:B:Cash  decomposition:   R&D–intensive  versus  non-R&D–intensive  firms.Table
49:1514:100711:24:24:72:540:250:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:8  reports  the  evolution  of  the  average  cash-to-assets  ratio  for  R&D–intensive  and  non-
49:1515:100809:24:24:72:540:226:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:R&D–intensive firms over the period 1979–2013. For each firm category, we separate between
49:1516:100899:24:24:72:540:202:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:firms that have entered the Compustat database within five years and firms that have been
49:1517:100988:24:40:72:340:178:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the Compustat database for more than five years.
49:1518:101039:40:24:72:540:138:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:B:The exit margin.Figure 12 compares the average cash holdings of entering and exiting
49:1519:101123:24:24:72:540:114:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:firms  in  our  sample.   The  data  show  that  exitors  hold  almost  the  same  cash  ratio  as  the
49:1520:101226:24:24:72:540:90:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:average firm over time, supporting the assumption of an exogenous and i.i.d.  exit process
49:1521:101316:24:0:72:167:66:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:used in the model.
50:1522:101336:0:24:72:540:721:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:B:Post-entry  dynamics.What  happens  to  cash  holdings  in  the  subsequent  years  after
50:1523:101425:24:24:72:539:697:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:entry?  Figure 13shows the differences in basic firm characteristics at entry (cash,  R&D,
50:1524:101515:24:24:72:540:673:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tangibility, and net leverage) persist over time.  That is, high R&D firms’ characteristics do
50:1525:101609:24:24:72:328:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:not converge to the levels held by low R&D firms.
50:1526:101658:24:23:89:539:625:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The  figure  shows  cash  holdings  for  entrants  from  the  entry  year  (year  0)  up  to  five
50:1527:101756:23:24:72:540:602:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:years  after  entry  (year  5)  together  with  other  key  firm-level  characteristics.   Both  high
50:1528:101857:24:24:72:540:578:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:R&D–intensive  and  low-R&D–intensive  firms  deplete  their  cash  holdings  after  the  entry
50:1529:101952:24:24:72:540:554:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:year.  The difference in average cash holdings between the two set of firms decreases during
50:1530:102044:24:24:72:540:530:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the first two years after entry and then stays constant around 0.18.  The R&D activity for
50:1531:102134:24:24:72:540:506:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:R&D–intensive firms stays constant during the five years after entry and fluctuates around
50:1532:102224:24:24:72:540:482:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:0.11, whereas low-R&D firms’ post-entry R&D investment fluctuates around 0.5% of total
50:1533:102310:24:24:72:105:458:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:assets.
50:1534:102317:24:24:89:539:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Both categories of firms show an increase in their post-entry values for tangibility and
50:1535:102405:24:24:72:540:410:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:net  leverage.   However,  these  values  are  highly  persistent  and  the  difference  at  the  entry
50:1536:102508:24:24:72:540:386:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:stage  remains  stable  for  the  entire  post-entry  period.   In  short,  R&D–intensive  and  non-
50:1537:102608:24:23:72:540:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:R&D–intensive firms do not converge in terms of key firm characteristics linked to production
50:1538:102701:23:24:72:540:339:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and financing structure.  This evidence supports our modeling decision of having a fixed type
50:1539:102794:24:0:72:462:315:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of firms rather than assuming firms that can dynamically change their type.
